  190. I've been using Sonicare electric toothbrushes for many years and have nothing but positive things to say about them; the Phillips Sonicare Essence 5600 is no different.<br /><br />This is the fourth Sonicare brush I've had. The other 3 are the FlexCare, Healthy White, and the older Elite models. The Essence 5600 is similar in design to the Elite series brushes. It has a larger body and a screw on type brush head. The major advantage this model has over all the other models I've owned is that it has stronger action in the brush head. My teeth feel like they get a more thorough cleaning when using this brush.<br /><br />A cool feature for anyone new to using an electric toothbrush is the Ramp-up mode. This allows your gums to slowly get adjusted to the action of the brush head over the first twelve uses. My first electric toothbrush didn't have this feature and it took me awhile to get used to it.<br /><br />Another plus is that it's convenient for traveling. The Essence 5600 lasts up to two weeks on a single charge and also comes with a cloth carrying pouch.<br /><br />The biggest disadvantage for me is the design of the brush head. Fluids are more prone to collect in the bottom part of the head between the body and where the head screws on. My FlexCare and Healthy White brushes attach to the body right at the base of the neck so fluid doesn't collect on the inside. With the Essence 5600, I have to clean out fluids twice as often.<br /><br />Despite this issue, I'd still recommend this product. The Sonicare Essence 5600 is a solid performer.

  270. This is the latest version of the original Sonicare design, where each replacement of the brush head comes with a new set of magnets. It's easy to see how the power of the brushing improves when you put on a new head. The fresh magnets are as important as the fresh bristles. The alternating magnetic field that vibrates the brush also slowly weakens the magnets. Getting fresh magnets with each head keeps the unit working like new,<br /><br />People complaining about this brush head design don't appreciate how it is required to maintain the brush performance. It's a feature, not a bug. I'm glad Sonicare has kept this basic design available.<br /><br />Rinsing out the brush and handle assembly after each use isn't all that burdensome, either: it takes less than 30 seconds, and is easily done as you give the unit the same kind of rinse you would give any toothbrush after use.<br /><br />Bottom line: this design is relatively cheap and easy to use while being highly effective. It has been a good replacement for my original Sonicare.

  455. Overall, the Sonicare Essence 5600 is an excellent basic electric toothbrush. The Essence 5600 just has an on/off switch and a 2-minute timer. In my opinion, these features are sufficient for most people. Other models have slightly more features. For example, I use a Sonicare HealthyWhite 3 Mode toothbrush, which has a setting for Clean, Sensitive, and Clean and White. You can actually hear and feel the difference at the different settings, e.g., the sensitive setting doesn't vibrate as vigorously as the clean setting. The vibration of the Essence 5600 is like the vibration on the \\"Clean\\" setting on my toothbrush.<br /><br />There are two things I don't like about the Essence 5600. First, it costs more to replace the brush heads. A 3-pack of brush heads for my HealthyWhite is cheaper than a 2-pack of brush heads for the Essence 5600.<br /><br />Second, the Essence 5600 is not compact relative to other electric toothbrushes. (1) The Essence 5600 is just big in almost every respect especially compared to my HealthyWhite. First, the handle itself is much larger in diameter. (2) The brush head is also big (as it includes the dome shaped connector to the body of the toothbrush). (3) The charger is also bigger because the HealthyWhite came with a separate travel charger that was really compact. (4) The travel case for the Essence 5600 is a soft case, which is unlike the HealthyWhite's hard case. Although the Essence 5600's case is smaller, the hard case for the HealthyWhite allows you to carry two brush heads.

It's what I will call the 'basic' model and I consider my 'weekend house' toothbrush. I also have the [[ASIN:B0019ZGU1S Philips Sonicare HX6732/02 HealthyWhite R732 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]], a 'deluxe' version, that I consider my day-to-day Sonicare. Both units are the cr&egrave;me of the crop tools when it comes to cleaning teeth. What sets the 'basic' model apart from my 'deluxe' Sonicare is seemingly minor, but is worth mentioning. To appreciate the difference, you have to know how you use the brush.<br /><br />To properly use Sonicare, you use it for 2 minutes. Exactly 2 minutes. 30 seconds on the top teeth on the outside, 30 second on the top teeth on the inside of your mouth, 30 seconds on the bottom teeth on the outside, and finally 30 seconds on the bottom teeth on the inside of your mouth.<br /><br />The 'deluxe' model has a small 'beep' every 30 seconds to keep you on track. The 'basic' model has no beep, no cues to keep you moving along. It seems minor, and in the scheme of life, it is. It's just that I really find my self *wanting* that feature on the 'basic' model. It's just not there. This seems like a fairly arbitrary omission on Philips' part. This omission is the only reason I have given this brush 4 stars instead of 5.<br /><br />There are some cosmetic differences between the 2 units. The 'basic' unit is heavier than the 'deluxe' model. Lastly, you can't share brush heads between these 2 units because they have different connectors at the base of the brush heads.<br /><br />I prefer the more expensive model, but for double the price, I'm not sure its 'must-have' feature I find so valuable in the more expensive model should sway you to the more expensive version. You may not miss it at all. Especially if I hadn't told you about it.   544. We bought our 3rd Sonicare after the first worked itself to death (old A series lasted for 3 or 4 years) and second (E series) pooped out before it was 2 years old. And we all love the way it keeps our teeth feeling as clean as our dentist hygienist used to do. In fact we can go longer between teeth cleanings and those done are much less extensive.<br /><br />One important point I want to bring to everyone's attention is how the charging instructions in the manual are WRONG! The manual says to leave the handle in the charging unit. Doing this will effectively 'pattern' the battery to where it will hold less and less of a charge. The 3rd replacement we recently bought is a 2 handle one that we charged for first 24 hours and then used - without recharging - over 60, 2 min. uses before it would not work for 2 mins. We then switched out the first handle for a totally charged second handle that is then used for another 60-ish uses. If you don't charge totally up and then discharge totally DOWN, the batteries will become less able to hold a long charge and you will be replacing a lot sooner than you would otherwise. Perhaps that is why the manual says to keep it in the charging unit?! Hmmmm!

I jumped at the opportunity to try out the Sonicare HX5610/01 electric toothbrush and after using it for about a month I have mixed feelings on the product.<br /><br />First, this toothbrush is really designed for a single person or for an individual who travels. This isn't really a practical toothbrush for more than an individual simply because there's no place to store an extra toothbrush head. I'm coming from using an Oral B electric toothbrush that had slots for storing more than one brush-head and was immediately disappointed that there isn't a similar feature here.<br /><br />Second this is a very basic electric toothbrush. For $70 you're getting a single function electric toothbrush, simply meaning that there's only an on/off button and no variable speed brushing or vibrating. There's a built in 2-minute timer that's the norm for electric toothbrushes; a charger; and a small storage bag. That's absolutely it. The toothbrush itself seems to be either poorly designed or just an early design that's never been improved upon. The major problem that I see with this brush is that water and toothpaste trickle down the handle and get inside the housing. After using this brush for a few days it left a mess of old toothpaste on the charger and my bathroom counter. Not only is this gross but I can't imagine toothpaste and water trickling down the inner components of this brush being very good for longevity.<br /><br />Lastly I was floored that this new Sonicare is not only heavier and bulkier than my 6 year old Oral B electric toothbrush but also considerably louder. Brushing with this thing is like standing on a subway platform as a train flies by; in other words a jarring experience.<br /><br />I would definitely not recommend this product. The brush runs two minutes and then shuts off. Use the brush two minutes for the top and two minutes for the bottom.   642. I'm not going to cover the merits of using a Sonicare electric toothbrush. Just use them. Plain and simple. You will save more in dental costs than you will spend on them. I have been using them for probably over 15 years, and they are must-haves. Everyone in my family uses them. I have also used every major generation of Sonicare toothbrush and several models within each.<br /><br />This Essence 5600 is styled like the original first generation. Unlike the first generation which used NiCad batteries, this uses NiMH batteries which was used in the second generation. The original first generation toothbrushes used an open sort of toothbrush head with a plate behind the brush. This was actually a good head, although it rattled/buzzed if you made the little plastic guard/plate touch the moving brush head. No big deal. With these you occasionally had to unscrew the head and clean them out (with an old-style toothbrush).<br /><br />However, Philips/Sonicare has discontinued the original style head and gone with a \\"universal\\" head that fits both the first and second generation toothbrushes. That is what you get with this model. Unfortunately, despite the more effective and more comfortable head, these are plagued with the problem of mold, bacteria, and just general funk under the rubber seal. The rubber seal just doesn't seal at all. Moisture gets in the heads, and shortly, there will be massive black and pink hairy things growing inside. Just truly disgusting which is why you see some aftermarket (non-Philips) seals being sold. Further, it is just next to impossible to clean these second generation heads. See my remedy at the end.<br /><br />The third generation (current) is truly the best. They went with Li-Ion batteries. The handles are smaller. The heads no longer have a \\"compartment\\" in which to grow mold and bacteria.<br /><br />Unfortunately, with the progression of each model, Sonicare keeps adding more features which I don't like. I find quad pacer useless and annoying. All of the additional massage and pulsing modes and what-not are just irritating because it makes such a simple device much harder to use. For example, instead of a simple on/off, you now have to push the button twice or cycle through these modes. This is important because if you push a button twice to cycle it and turn it off while it is in the middle of changing modes, instead of it turning off, it turns on, and your spit and toothpaste go flying, so now you have to clean your glasses, the mirror, and pretty much everything within 3 feet.<br /><br />Anyway, sorry to digress, but I have UNIVERSALLY found that the best model with in each generation is the most simple one without all the feature-laden whistles and bells, ridiculous UV cleaners, etc., which just drive up your cost both initial and in consumables.<br /><br />So, in sum, this has good battery technology, but you will have to be careful not to leave it in the charger and make sure you run it down. In other words, you will have to run it like a usual Ni-MH battery product to get the maximum life of maybe 3-5 years. If you don't, then you can kill it is 1-2 years. I like that this is a simple version and easy to operate. It has a nice grip and travel pouch. It it also is relatively inexpensive if you are new to Sonicare, but your next one will want to be the Li-Ion versions. What I really don't like about this is the terrible toothbrush heads which get funky. My best recommendation for dealing with this is as follows. (Disclaimer: this is not recommended or supported by the manufacturer. Use at your own risk, yada, yada.) Get some small, sharp scissors or a box cutter or utility knife and cut off that rubber seal -- which doesn't seal anyway. Then, after you brush your teeth just run some water down in there to rinse it out. Without the seal, it will dry, and not get so funky. At least 10X better, although it looks kinda MacGyver'ed.

  706. This brush has what I consider a serious design flaw that creates a very unsanitary situation. The \\"green police\\" have convinced Phillips that when the battery gives out, the owner should take the handle apart to dispose of the batteries. To allow the handle to be broken open there is a slot for a screw driver to be used as a pry bar to break the seal between the halves. The seal is on the inner margins of the halves leaving a slot on each side running the length of the handle. This slot is 3-4 thousandths wide and at least that deep. There's the problem. After using the brush, I always wash it off an dry the surface thoroughly before retiring it to the charging cradle. I did this with the new brush after a 24 hour change. The next morning when I picked up the brush, the cradle was stuck to it. When I pulled the handle out there was a sticky material in the cradle. I cleaned it all out, but the next day the same material was there. I assumed there was a defect and sent it back to Amazon. The replacement arrive in a day, but the same sticky situation occurred. I called customer service, but it took three or four days to connect. They could not account for the problem, but offered to send me another handle. While waiting for the handle to arrive and after finding the \\"'goo\\" was tooth paste, I realized that the water and tooth paste got into the slot, but cannot be cleaned out. Once standing in the cradle, the liquid settles downwind by gravity and ends up the gooey mess in the cradle. I e-mailed customer service with my findings and complaint. They were polite, but showed no concern. They gave me the name of someone to whom I could lodge a complaint. I haven't bothered, as I'm sure it would be a waste of time. I wonder if anyone there reads the reviews here. Similar problems has been seen and reported! I sent the second handle back and on the third handle used silicone sealant to fill the slot, hopefully solving the problem. The bacteria in the human mouthare an ugly bunch. Human bites area very bad. Collecting and storing saliva in your tooth brush is not good. Phillips should correct this. If this was an automobile, there's be a recall !! I do not recommend this model. Addendum: I used silicone to seal the openings Solved the problem. No more drainage in the charging cradle.

  776. I am also surprised Sonicare is still making this model. I have owned Sonicares for years, probably bought 6-7 of them and my whole family has them. There have been several generations of Sonicare, and up until the most recent generation, they had two critical flaws in my book, and this model shares those flaws: (1) they only work on 110v - so if you travel outside the Americas, you have to carry a heavy converter (not adapter, voltage converter) or else they burn out and (2) the brush head is poorly designed so that water and saliva goes down into a reservoir inside which becomes a gunky stinky mess. The entry level new design corrects both of these problems and is available on Amazon for about $10 more than this one -- and well worth it. It's called the Sonicare Easy Clean.   777. Sonicare likes to keep this style around to offer more affordable entry into the Sonicare toothbrush line. It is a bit surprising that this larger model with the older style brush head connection is still around and being sold as new. Compared to the older version this model does offer a travel pack and better grip, but doesn't seem to offer much else new. Regardless of that, Sonicare is still my favorite when it comes to electric toothbrushes and this version is a good value even with the older design. For those not wanting to spend a lot on a brush this version offers long batter life, two minute timer, charging indicator, and travel pouch. If you are new to Sonicare just remember one thing, the replacement heads are not cheap compared to the actual cost of the whole Sonicare brush itself. Obviously Phillips money making is in the replaceable heads and not in the actual selling of the brush.<br /><br />The one thing I do not like about this style of brush is the head connection itsef. Water and toothpaste can get into the head connection and it gets kind of nasty looking after a while. My wife uses this one style and she has to flush out the head connection with hot water to get all of that out, or replace the head itself. I have the thinner higher priced whitening model and it does not have this design so I do not have to wash out the head connection.<br /><br />One thing to keep in mind when you are considering one is the cost of this model compared to the thinner, lighter, and better designed higher priced models. If you travel a lot having the thinner model might be the way to go as the batter still lasts over 7 days and it is easier and lighter to carry.

For as long as I can remember my gums have bled after brushing my teeth, even when brushing by hand. Instead of replacing just the brush on the stem [[ASIN:B000WHNI2I Philips Sonicare HX6013/90 ProResults Brush Head Standard, 3-Pack]] you have to replace the whole top part [[ASIN:B0046AAVR2 Philips Sonicare HX7002/30 e-Series Replacement Brush Heads, 2-Pack (Frustration Free Packaging)]] which is more difficult to unscrew and replace. It also is more difficult to clean because it doesn't just pull out like my old one, and it's possible to get fluids under this brush base so you do have to clean it. The whole toothbrush isn't as compact as my older model either. The charging base is larger and the handle of the brush is wider. What I do like better about this model is that the movement is a little stronger than my older model, the brush seems to move faster and have a little more power. I think it cleans my teeth faster. It stops after 2 minutes and you have to restart it again if you want to continue. (Why does 2 minutes seem so long when you're in a hurry?) My older model had little pauses that you could hear after each 30 seconds so you knew how long you were spending on each part of your mouth (Quadpacer Technology). This model doesn't have that, but I didn't really pay that much attention to it anyway. Both are easy to take along when you travel. This one has a nice little carrying case. Once it's charged it will last for up to 2 weeks without being in the charger base. I don't know how long the older one would hold a charge because it was compact enough to take the whole thing along when we traveled so I never let the charge run down.<br /><br />So I guess my rating would actually be a 4-1/2. I like that it seems a little more powerful than my [[ASIN:B0019ZEVZU Philips Sonicare HX6711/02 HealthyWhite 710 Rechargeable Electric Toothbrush]] but I don't like that the brush assembly is more expensive to replace and more difficult to disassemble and clean. Does it get my teeth whiter than the old model? Well, my teeth are probably as white as they are going to get because I think that all Philips Sonicare brushes do an excellent job so I don't see a difference between the two models in how they clean.
